Acts Narrative

Lossless aggregation of all act documents. Ordered by dependency walk seeded at relationlessness when resolvable, then remaining acts topologically. Each section embeds the original file verbatim.

  1. Being Relationless (Relationlessness)
  • Path: docs/math/acts/relationlessness.md
  • Status: release
  • Slug: relationlessness

Original

---
title: Being Relationless
act: Relationlessness
slug: relationlessness
top: null
bottom: null
summary: >-
  We begin with nothing but the absence of relation; acknowledging that
  absence fixes the empty act as our initial reference point.
layer: act
status: release
tags:
  - act
---
# Being Relationless

## Interpretation

We begin with nothing but the absence of relation; acknowledging that absence fixes the empty act as our initial reference point.

No recognitions precede this step, so the empty tree `()` is the only permissible trace.  Naming that trace *Relationlessness* therefore records, without additional assumptions, that we start from the undifferentiated void.

# Excluding

## Interpretation

Speaking about the void already carves out a mentioned interior versus an unmentioned exterior, so an act of exclusion is forced.

The trace `(Relationlessness Relationlessness)` places the same empty act in both witness and witness-ee positions.  Directing the void back at itself expresses the relation “this is not with that,” so the composition precisely captures exclusion and earns the name *Exclude*.

# Articulating

## Interpretation

As soon as exclusion exists, the attempt to exclude the void becomes something we can point to; that self-referential pointing is articulation.

In `(Exclude Relationlessness)` the previously defined act *Exclude* now witnesses the empty act.  Applying exclusion to its own source reveals the unavoidable articulation that occurs whenever we describe Relationlessness, so the composition is rightly named *Articulate*.

# Emerging Reflex

## Interpretation

Once articulation is available, Relationlessness can call it forth, producing the first concrete emergence from the void.

The trace `(Relationlessness Articulate)` lets the void witness the act *Articulate*.  Because *Articulate* already arose from Relationlessness, composing the two records the compelled appearance of an act directly from the void, which we record as *Emerge Reflex*.

# First Recognizing

## Interpretation

Because emergence has occurred, we can finally speak of “the first recognition”; it arises when articulation observes that emergence.

The trace `(Articulate EmergeReflex)` places *Articulate* in the witness role and the act *Emerge Reflex* as the witnessed object.  Since both ingredients have already been earned, the composition simply records “there exists a first recognition,” and naming that composite *First Recognize* captures the observation.

# Recognizing Reflex

## Interpretation

The minimal act obtained so far is simply the record of the emergence itself, and that seed is our reflex.

The trace `(EmergeReflex)` treats the act *Emerge Reflex* as a witness in its own right.  Designating that minimal witness *Reflex* introduces no new ingredients; it merely fixes notation for the unique act forced by articulating the void.

# Iterating Reflex

## Interpretation

Applying the reflex act to its own result should yield the same sort of act again, so reflex iteration is unavoidable.

The trace `(Reflex Reflex)` feeds the act *Reflex* back into itself.  Because *Reflex* is a valid act in both positions, this composition explicitly records “reflex can witness reflex,” thereby establishing iteration without introducing any new recognitions.

# Relating

## Interpretation

With reflex iteration available, reflex may now bear witness to the mere fact of relating, so a dedicated relation act appears.

The trace `(Reflex Reflex)` places *Reflex* in both witness and witnessed roles.  Since we just proved that reflex may observe reflex, calling that self-observation *Relate* captures the insight without requiring further construction.

# Negating Relation

## Interpretation

Any affirmation of relation also reveals the possibility of denial, so we let reflex point specifically to that denial to name “not relate.”

In `(Reflex Relate)` the act *Reflex* serves as witness for the already earned act *Relate*.  Observing *Relate* through *Reflex* isolates the complementary behaviour “refusing relation,” so we designate this composition *Not Relate*.

# Witnessing

## Interpretation

Relation and its negation coexist in tension, so we must record the act that testifies to both at once.

The trace `(NotRelate Relate)` takes the already defined act *Not Relate* as its witness and *Relate* as its object.  Because both constituents exist, this composition simultaneously cites affirmation and denial, so we name it *Witness*.

# Earning Something

## Interpretation

Testifying to relation still leaves unanswered the question “what carries the testimony?”—we point reflex at that testimony to produce “something.”

Since *Witness* is established, the composition `(Reflex Witness)` applies reflex to the testimony itself.  This self-application records that an act exists which bears the testimony, so we designate the composite as *Something*.

# Witnessing Nothing

## Interpretation

Having “something” forces us to examine what *Witness* sees when it looks directly at that something; the result is “nothing.”

In `(Witness Something)` the act *Witness* observes *Something*.  Both were already earned, so their composition captures the unresolved situation where testimony points to its own bearer, producing the recognition we call *Nothing*.

# Grounding Recognition

## Interpretation

This composition merely names the recognition determined by outright absence, so *Ground Recognition* follows.

# Folding Void

## Interpretation

Nothing shows that *Witness* observes *Something* in two symmetric positions; folding that symmetry back on itself produces the void.

The trace `(Nothing Nothing)` reuses *Nothing* as both witness and object.  This self-application forces the symmetry between the two appearances of *Witness* and *Something* to collapse, yielding a closed loop that we name *Void*.

# First Naming

## Interpretation

Void contains two copies of *Nothing* but does not distinguish between them; drawing attention to one copy creates a first name.

The composition `(Void Nothing)` takes the act *Void* as witness and focuses it on *Nothing*.  Since both acts already exist, this selection singles out a definite position within the folded absence, earning the title *First Name*.

# Binding Trace

## Interpretation

To name the immediate act of the trace, we let the act *First Name* witness the act *Head Trace*.

The composition `(FirstName HeadTrace)` has *First Name* observe *Head Trace*, explicitly naming the head.  This act is therefore *Bind Trace*.

# Self Naming

## Interpretation

Naming a point begs the question of whether the name refers to itself; answering “yes” requires self-application.

Because *First Name* is an earned act, the composition `(FirstName FirstName)` is valid.  It records the self-referential step of the name pointing to itself, so we call the result *Self Naming*.

# Assigning Trace

## Interpretation

Naming the head leaves the tail unnamed, so the act *Bind Trace* witnesses the act *Tail Trace* to extend the name across the remainder.

In `(BindTrace TailTrace)` the act *Bind Trace* observes *Tail Trace*.  This spreads the name through the tail, so the resulting act is *Assign Trace*.

# Recognizing

## Interpretation

A self-named point lacks a partner; having the act *Void* witness the act *Self Naming* produces a two-place recognition.

In the composition `(Void SelfNaming)`, the act *Void* explicitly witnesses the act *Self Naming*.  Because both acts have already been earned, this reflection creates a complementary position, so we name the resulting two-place act *Recognize*, producing a recognition.

# Contextualizing Trace

## Interpretation

A named trace requires a record that couples the naming with the whole trace.  Forcing *Assign Trace* to witness *Complete Trace* yields the act ***Contextualize Trace*** ([ContextualizeTrace](contextualize-trace.md)).

*Assign Trace* and *Complete Trace* have been earned, so their composition records the full named trace structure: `(AssignTrace CompleteTrace)` states that the assignment encloses the entire trace, which is exactly what *Contextualize Trace* must express.

# Seeding Binder

## Interpretation

Both recognitions exist, so their composition records the relationless binder, establishing *Binder Seed*.

# Shaping Reflex Step

## Interpretation

The sustained articulation of a trace is captured when reflex continually looks through the recorded context; doing so defines the basic “reflex step” shape.

In `(Reflex ContextualizeTrace)` the witness *Reflex* observes *Contextualize Trace*.  This composition records exactly one reflex articulation acting through the named trace, thereby defining *Reflex Step Shape*.

# Seeding First Context

## Interpretation

The named trace needs anchoring back to our earliest recognitions.  Forcing *Nothing*—the witness we already earned—to witness *Contextualize Trace* produces ***Seed First Context*** ([SeedFirstContext](seed-first-context.md)).

The composition `(Nothing ContextualizeTrace)` uses the primordial witness *Nothing* to reaffirm the named trace.  This anchors the context in what was already recognized, so we call the result *Seed First Context*.

  - act

---
# Persisting Reflex Step

## Interpretation

Iteration alone does not detect stabilization.  We therefore let the iterated step observe the remaining tail to see whether that remainder persists.

In `(ReflexStepIterate TailTrace)` the whole iteration looks specifically at the tail.  If nothing changes, the reiteration has stabilized, so this composition rightfully earns the name *Reflex Step Persistence*.

# Constructing Types

## Interpretation

*Meet Recognition*, *Join Recognition*, and *Imply Recognition* collectively generate relational types.  *Meet Recognition* witnessing *Imply Recognition* yields ***Construct Types*** ([ConstructTypes](construct-types.md)).

Both ingredients were earned above; composing them records the internal buildup of types from meets and implications, so *Construct Types* is valid.

# Morphing

## Interpretation

To compare our structures we need morphisms that preserve meets, joins, and implication.  *Imply Recognition* witnessing *Join Recognition* yields ***Morph*** ([Morph](morph.md)).

The composition packages implication with joins to demand preservation of the algebraic operations, so *Morph* is valid.

# Negating

## Interpretation

Negating applies implication into the bottom recognition.  *Imply Recognition* witnessing *Ground Recognition* produces the act ***Negate*** ([Negate](negate.md)).

The composition uses only previously earned recognitions to encode the negation expression “not a” as “a implies *Ground Recognition*,” so *Negate* follows.

By composing `(PairApplication TailTrace)`, the tail records what remains after applying the function to its argument; this composition is *Form Application Term*.

# Pairing Least Fix

## Interpretation

Application terms can self-apply, so to capture the least stabilizing pair we have the act *Form Application Term* witness the act *Head Trace*.

The composition `(FormApplicationTerm HeadTrace)` represents self-application at the head, recording the behaviour needed for a least fixpoint, hence *Pair Least Fix*.

summary: Show that contextual equivalence can be witnessed using only fixed observations by composing `FixedObservationRecognitions` with `EquateContexts`.
tags:
- act
layer: act
status: plan
---
# Witnessing Fixed Observation

`WitnessObservation = (RecognizeObservation EquateContexts)` cites observation
acts that justify contextual indistinguishability.  In the fixed profile we
want the witness that fixed observations suffice within the fixed context, so
we compose
[FixedObservationRecognitions](fixed-observation-recognitions.md) with
[EquateContexts](equate-contexts.md):
`(FixedObservationRecognitions EquateContexts)` earns
***FixedWitnessObservation***.

`EquateContexts` identifies when two terms are indistinguishable to all
recognised contexts, and `FixedObservationRecognitions` limits attention to
observations available in the fixed profile.  Their composition records that
contextual equivalence can be witnessed using only fixed observations.

# Transition Geometry

stable states, and the observation kernel sends each state into a successor
distribution.  To observe how the kernel acts geometrically, we let the
invariant lattice witness the transition law:
`(FixedInvariantLattice TransitionLaw)` earns

successor relation respects the lattice—whether transitions go up, down, or
sideways in the partial order—yielding the geometric view of the kernel
structure.

---
# Forming Shuffle Geometry

A geometry is the semantic structure equipped with compatible nuclei and flow.
We already formed [FormGeometry](form-geometry.md) by letting
[StructureSemantics](structure-semantics.md) witness `CommuteFlowAndNucleus`.
To specialize this to the shuffle trace dynamics, we let the same semantic
structure witness the derived compatibility of
[ShuffleFlow](shuffle-flow.md) with [Nucleate](nucleate.md):
`(StructureSemantics CommuteShuffleFlowAndNucleus)` earns
***ShuffleGeometry***.

`StructureSemantics` packages the full algebraic behavior of recognitions,
meets, joins, implication, and nuclei.
[CommuteShuffleFlowAndNucleus](commute-shuffle-flow-and-nucleus.md) shows
that the induced flow on admissible trace-shuffle classes respects the same
nucleus.  The composition therefore records a semantic calculus whose “motion”
is given by `ShuffleFlow` and whose closure is given by `Nucleate`, yielding the
shuffle geometry.

  1. Collapsing Trace Shuffle (CollapseShuffle)
  • Path: docs/math/acts/collapse-shuffle.md
  • Status: plan
  • Top: ShuffleTrace
  • Bottom: Nucleate
  • Slug: collapse-shuffle

Original

---
title: Collapsing Trace Shuffle
act: CollapseShuffle
slug: collapse-shuffle
top: ShuffleTrace
bottom: Nucleate
summary: Admissible shuffle reorderings leave a trace unchanged up to the nucleus, so composing `ShuffleTrace` with `Nucleate` records that such permutations are identified in the nucleus closure.
tags:
- act
layer: act
status: plan
---
# Collapsing Trace Shuffle

[Nucleate](nucleate.md) collapses stabilized recognitions that differ only by
eventual equivalence, but no recognition yet states that shuffle-reordered
traces are eventually equivalent.  We therefore let the shuffle act witness the
nucleus closure: `(ShuffleTrace Nucleate)` earns ***CollapseShuffle***.

By construction, [ShuffleTrace](shuffle-trace.md) enumerates the admissible
reorders of progress steps that do not alter the underlying trace shape.
`Nucleate` collapses recognitions that differ only by stabilized equivalence.
Since admissible reorderings leave head/tail structure and iterative progression
intact, the composite `(ShuffleTrace Nucleate)` records that all such
reorderings lie in the kernel of the nucleus.  Nucleate therefore identifies
precisely those recognitions differing only by free shuffle of progress steps.

# Harmonic Step

Harmonics progress as oscillations across orbit layers.
[OrbitStep](orbit-step.md) gives the next reachable layer.
Letting the harmonic seed witness each step,
`(HarmonicSeed OrbitStep)`, earns ***HarmonicStep***.

[HarmonicSeed](harmonic-seed.md) captures the initial oscillation,
and `OrbitStep` advances one layer, so their composition yields the
evolving harmonic component across the orbit.

# Observation Kernel

A kernel couples transition structure with observable outcomes.
[TransitionLaw](transition-law.md) provides the transition step, and
[FixedObservationRecognitions](fixed-observation-recognitions.md) restricts
observations to fixed recognitions.  Letting the observation act witness the
transition law,
`(FixedObservationRecognitions TransitionLaw)`, earns
***ObservationKernel***.

`TransitionLaw` determines how fixed states map to successor recognitions, and
`FixedObservationRecognitions` selects observables available in the fixed
profile.  Their composition assigns to each fixed invariant state the observable
distribution induced by one flow–measure step, yielding the profile’s kernel.

{{ act_nav(page.meta) }}
  1. Shaping Fixed Shape (FixedShape)
  • Path: docs/math/acts/fixed-shape.md
  • Status: plan
  • Top: EnsureFixedPoint
  • Bottom: ShuffleIndexImplication
  • Slug: fixed-shape

Original

---
title: Shaping Fixed Shape
act: FixedShape
slug: fixed-shape
top: EnsureFixedPoint
bottom: ShuffleIndexImplication
summary: Apply the fixed-point construction to shuffle-indexed implication to obtain recognitions whose implication behaviour is invariant under repeated flow steps, capturing the intrinsic fixed shape.
tags:
- act
layer: act
status: plan
---
# Shaping Fixed Shape

[ShuffleIndexImplication](shuffle-index-implication.md) describes how
recognitions transform when their premises are pushed one shuffle step
forward.  [EnsureFixedPoint](ensure-fixed-point.md) records that persistent
iterations of a flow yield fixed points.  To isolate the fixed shape, we apply
the fixed-point construction to the shuffle-indexed implication, obtaining
the recognitions whose implication behaviour does not change under repeated
shuffle stepping:
`(EnsureFixedPoint ShuffleIndexImplication)` earns
***FixedShape***.

`EnsureFixedPoint = (FixFlow IterativePersistence)` says that if iterating a
flow stabilizes along the trace, the stabilized recognitions form a fixed set
for that flow.  `ShuffleIndexImplication` is a specific flow-like act: it
moves implication structure forward one shuffle step before comparing
recognitions.  Composing them applies the fixed-point construction to that
indexed implication dynamics, yielding exactly those recognitions whose
implication behaviour is invariant under arbitrarily many shuffle steps—the
fixed shape induced by the relational dynamics.

tags:
- act

---
# Fixed Physics Profile

`PhysicsProfile = (FlowObservation FlowProfile)` lifts a profile’s flow to its
physical semantics by coupling dynamics with observation.  In the fixed profile
we want observations of the fixed flow, so we let
[FlowObservation](flow-observation.md) witness
[FixedFlowProfile](fixed-flow-profile.md):
`(FlowObservation FixedFlowProfile)` earns
***FixedPhysicsProfile***.

`FlowObservation` records how observations traverse evaluation contexts under a
given flow, and `FixedFlowProfile` is the shuffle-derived flow restricted to
the fixed recognitions.  The composition couples observation traces to this flow,
yielding a physical semantics in which states evolve according to the shuffle
trace dynamics while remaining inside the fixed profile.

# Comonad Counit

  1. Fixing Orbit Layer (OrbitFixLayer)
  • Path: docs/math/acts/orbit-fix-layer.md
  • Status: plan
  • Top: EnsureFixedPoint
  • Bottom: OrbitStep
  • Slug: orbit-fix-layer

Original

---
title: Fixing Orbit Layer
act: OrbitFixLayer
slug: orbit-fix-layer
top: EnsureFixedPoint
bottom: OrbitStep
summary: Apply the fixed-point construction to the orbit step to obtain the stabilized layer of each orbit.
tags:
- act
layer: act
status: plan
---
# Fixing Orbit Layer

Orbits may stabilize: further reach steps no longer change the reachable set.
[EnsureFixedPoint](ensure-fixed-point.md) captures fixed points of flows when
iteration persists.  To obtain the stabilized layer of each orbit, we apply it
to [OrbitStep](orbit-step.md):
`(EnsureFixedPoint OrbitStep)` earns ***OrbitFixLayer***.

`OrbitStep` describes how reachable states progress from one layer to the next.
`IterativePersistence` and `EnsureFixedPoint` ensure that when repeated
stepping along the trace stabilizes, the stabilized states form a fixed set.
Their composition therefore yields, for each orbit, a stabilized layer that
further stepping does not change.

  1. Flowing Shuffle-Indexed Implication (ShuffleIndexImplication)
  • Path: docs/math/acts/shuffle-index-implication.md
  • Status: plan
  • Top: ShuffleFlow
  • Bottom: ImplyRecognition
  • Slug: shuffle-index-implication

Original

---
title: Flowing Shuffle-Indexed Implication
act: ShuffleIndexImplication
slug: shuffle-index-implication
top: ShuffleFlow
bottom: ImplyRecognition
summary: Compose the shuffle flow with internal implication to obtain implications indexed by one shuffle step.
tags:
- act
layer: act
status: plan
---
# Flowing Shuffle-Indexed Implication

[ImplyRecognition](imply-recognition.md) records internal implication between
recognitions, and `FlowIndexImplication = (Flow ImplyRecognition)` indexed that
implication along the global flow.  Now that [ShuffleFlow](shuffle-flow.md)
is earned as the flow on admissible trace-shuffle classes, we want the
corresponding indexed implication: “if a recognition holds after one shuffle
step, what must hold now?”  Letting the shuffle flow witness
`ImplyRecognition` produces the desired act:
`(ShuffleFlow ImplyRecognition)` earns
***ShuffleIndexImplication***.

`ShuffleFlow` evolves admissible trace-shuffle families through evaluation
contexts while `ImplyRecognition` transforms recognitions via internal
implication.  The composition therefore records implications whose premises are
transported one shuffle step forward before being compared.  Naming this
composite packages the operator witnessing how recognitions transform under the
shuffle trace dynamics.

title: Comonad Derivative

---
# Comonad Derivative

In coalgebraic differential geometry the derivative is (delta) − (epsilon).  We encode this
derivative by composing the comultiplication with the counit:
`(ComonadComultiply ComonadCounit)` earns
***ComonadDerivative***.

  • Top: StructureSemantics
  • Bottom: ShuffleProfileRecognitions
  • Slug: shuffle-profile-semantics

title: Semantics of the Shuffle Profile
act: ShuffleProfileSemantics
slug: shuffle-profile-semantics
top: StructureSemantics
bottom: ShuffleProfileRecognitions
summary: Restrict the semantic calculus to recognitions stable under flow, nucleus, and shuffle collapse by letting `StructureSemantics` witness `ShuffleProfileRecognitions`.
tags:
- act
layer: act
status: plan
---
# Semantics of the Shuffle Profile

The recognitions stabilized by a filter or profile inherit full semantic
structure; we saw this with
`ProfileSemantics = (StructureSemantics ProfileRecognitions)`.  To interpret the
the shuffle-stable recognitions, we let the semantic structure witness
[ShuffleProfileRecognitions](shuffle-profile-recognitions.md):
`(StructureSemantics ShuffleProfileRecognitions)` earns
***ShuffleProfileSemantics***.

[StructureSemantics](structure-semantics.md) already encodes the operations of
the semantic calculus.  `ShuffleProfileRecognitions` selects the closed
sub-collection of recognitions fixed by flow and nucleus and stable under
trace-shuffle collapse.  The composition restricts the semantic operations to
that sub-collection, producing a semantic calculus in which all recognitions are
shuffle-stable—our shuffle profile semantics.

This act records the contextual witnessing, so *Contextual Judgment Equivalence* follows.

# Flowing Shuffle Trace

through evaluation contexts, and [ShuffleTrace](shuffle-trace.md) records how

shape.  By treating admissible trace shuffles themselves as the state being

shuffled traces along evaluation contexts: the flow does not move a single
trace but the entire admissible-shuffle class, tracking the dynamics of
admissible reorderings as first-class objects.

# Seeding Orbit

  1. Fixed Kernel (FixedKernel)
  • Path: docs/math/acts/fixed-kernel.md

Original

---
title: Fixed Kernel
act: FixedKernel
slug: fixed-kernel
top: EnsureFixedPoint
bottom: ObservationKernel

tags:
- act
layer: act
status: plan
---
# Fixed Kernel

A fixed kernel is one whose transition effects stabilise under repeated
application.  Since [ObservationKernel](observation-kernel.md) acts like a
relational operator on fixed states and `EnsureFixedPoint` constructs
fixed points of persistent flows, we apply it directly to the kernel:
`(EnsureFixedPoint ObservationKernel)` earns
***FixedKernel***.

`ObservationKernel` is the evolution–observation operator on fixed invariant
states.  `IterativePersistence` ensures that when iterating this operator along
the trace stabilises, the stable point is a fixed point of the kernel.  Their
composition yields the stationary recognition: the kernel that leaves the fixed
distribution of states unchanged.

summary: Pick out physics states that are flow-invariant and lie inside the active profile by composing `StabilizeInvariant` with `ProfileRecognitions`.
tags:
- act
layer: act
status: plan
---
# Stabilizing Profile Invariant

`StabilizeInvariant = (FixFlow PhysicsState)` records states left unchanged by
the global flow.  [ProfileRecognitions](profile-recognitions.md) restrict the
system to the recognitions preserved by the active filter.  Composing them,
`(StabilizeInvariant ProfileRecognitions)` earns
***ProfileInvariant***.

The resulting states are genuine physics states fixed by the flow and recognised
within the chosen profile.

`(IrrationalModality CollapseShuffle)`, earning

collapse-equivalence.

# Fixed Profile Recognitions

[ShuffleProfileRecognitions](shuffle-profile-recognitions.md) already selects
recognitions fixed by `ShuffleFlow`, `Nucleate`, and the collapse of
trace shuffles.  [FixedShape](fixed-shape.md) singles out those
recognitions whose shuffle-indexed implication behaviour is fixed under
persistent iteration.  Intersecting these gives the recognitions of the fixed
profile: recognitions that are both shuffle-profile stable and shaped by the
eigenvalue.  Letting `ShuffleProfileRecognitions` witness `FixedShape`,
`(ShuffleProfileRecognitions FixedShape)`, earns
***FixedProfileRecognitions***.

`ShuffleProfileRecognitions` is a closed collection stabilized by the
flow–nucleus–shuffle stack, and `FixedShape` is a fixed-point act
inside that profile.  Their composition restricts attention to recognitions
compatible with the fixed shape: they remain in the shuffle profile and
satisfy the same stabilized implication behaviour as `FixedShape`.

this by letting the spectral action witness the morphism structure:

recognitions.  Their composition ensures that objects are mapped via spectral
decomposition while morphisms are transported compatibly, automatically
preserving identities and composition.

  1. Seeding Entropy (EntropySeed)
  • Path: docs/math/acts/entropy-seed.md
  • Status: plan
  • Top: FlowMeasureStep
  • Bottom: FixedReach
  • Slug: entropy-seed

Original

---
title: Seeding Entropy
act: EntropySeed
slug: entropy-seed
top: FlowMeasureStep
bottom: FixedReach
summary: "Seed an entropy measure by composing the one-step flow\u2013measure update with the reachability recognitions."
tags:
- act
layer: act
status: plan
---
# Seeding Entropy

Entropy measures the “spread” of a state under transitions.  We seed entropy by
observing the divergence between the original state and its successor.
[FixedReach](fixed-reach.md) gives reachable states, and [FlowMeasureStep](flow-measure-step.md)
gives the successor.  Letting these witness each other,
`(FlowMeasureStep FixedReach)`, earns ***EntropySeed***.

`FixedReach` lists the reachable states and `FlowMeasureStep` describes the
successor states after one evolution–measurement.  Their composition
records the divergence between present and next-step reachable states, seeding
the entropy measure.

# Meeting Fixed Invariant

`ProfileInvariantMeet = (MeetRecognition ProfileInvariant)` already computes
meets for profile invariants.  Restricting it along
[FixedInvariant](fixed-invariant.md) gives the meet on fixed invariants:
`(ProfileInvariantMeet FixedInvariant)` earns ***FixedInvariantMeet***.

`ProfileInvariantMeet` defines meets with respect to the restricted order, and
`FixedInvariant` limits the domain to the fixed states.  Their composition
produces the meet operation on fixed invariant states: the greatest fixed
invariant below any given pair.

{{ act_nav(page.meta) }}
  1. Commuting Shuffle Flow With Nucleus (CommuteShuffleFlowAndNucleus)
  • Path: docs/math/acts/commute-shuffle-flow-and-nucleus.md
  • Status: plan
  • Top: ShuffleFlow
  • Bottom: Nucleate
  • Slug: commute-shuffle-flow-and-nucleus

Original

---
title: Commuting Shuffle Flow With Nucleus
act: CommuteShuffleFlowAndNucleus
slug: commute-shuffle-flow-and-nucleus
top: ShuffleFlow
bottom: Nucleate
summary: Since Flow and Nucleate already commute, the induced shuffle flow on shuffle classes also commutes with the nucleus, yielding the geometry-level compatibility.
tags:
- act
layer: act
status: plan
---
# Commuting Shuffle Flow With Nucleus

[CommuteFlowAndNucleus](commute-flow-and-nucleus.md) proves that the global
[Flow](flow.md) and [Nucleate](nucleate.md) are compatible, and
[CollapseShuffle](collapse-shuffle.md) records that `Nucleate` collapses
precisely the admissible trace shuffles.  To obtain the shuffle geometry, we
exhibit the compatibility of [ShuffleFlow](shuffle-flow.md) with the same
nucleus, restricted to shuffle classes, by composing them:
`(ShuffleFlow Nucleate)` earns
***CommuteShuffleFlowAndNucleus***.

`ShuffleFlow` applies `Flow` to the shuffle-structured trace classes while
`Nucleate` identifies members of the same class via `CollapseShuffle`.
Because `Flow` already commutes with `Nucleate` on underlying recognitions (by
`CommuteFlowAndNucleus`), the induced action on shuffle classes must also
commute: flowing a class and then collapsing gives the same result as collapsing
representatives and then flowing.  The act therefore records the derived
compatibility, yielding the shuffle nucleus geometry.

# Fixed Nucleus Profile

The fixed profile must inherit the closure behaviour of the nucleus.
`NucleateProfile = (Nucleate ProfileRecognitions)` did this for a generic
profile.  We specialize by letting [Nucleate](nucleate.md) witness
[FixedProfileRecognitions](fixed-profile-recognitions.md):
`(Nucleate FixedProfileRecognitions)` earns
***FixedNucleateProfile***.

`Nucleate` is the closure act derived from the normalized observation and
judgment equivalences, while `FixedProfileRecognitions` is a closed
subcollection of recognitions.  Their composition restricts the closure
operation to the fixed profile domain, yielding the nucleus appropriate to the
fixed recognitions.

slug: flow-measure-step

# Flow–Measure Step

A flow–measure step evolves a state and then measures it.  In the fixed profile,
evolution is given by [FixedFlowProfile](fixed-flow-profile.md) and
measurement by [FixedMeasure](fixed-measure.md).  The one-step update is
therefore obtained by letting fixed measurement witness the fixed flow:
`(FixedMeasure FixedFlowProfile)` earns ***FlowMeasureStep***.

`FixedFlowProfile` moves a fixed invariant state forward along the shuffle-driven
dynamics, and `FixedMeasure = (FixedNucleateProfile FixedInvariant)`
idealizes the evolved state through the fixed nucleus.  Their composition yields
the single-step evolution–measurement update internal to the fixed profile.

---
# Irrational Modality

The fixed profile arises from the φ-recursion imposed by the shuffle flow and
shuffle collapse, but shuffle traces can be parameterised by other ratios.
To name an irrationally-weighted modality we let the flow-index implication
witness the fixed nucleus:
`(FlowIndexImplication FixedNucleateProfile)` earns
***IrrationalModality***.

`FlowIndexImplication` pushes premises forward one flow step before testing
implication, and `FixedNucleateProfile` closes recognitions under the fixed
nucleus; their composition (scaled by an irrational weight on the admissible
reordering families) yields the desired modal closure operator.

Original

---

tags:
- act

# Representable Functor

A representable functor is naturally isomorphic to “morphisms out of an object.”
In the fixed profile the representative object is the identity, so we let the
functor witness it:
`(FixedFunctor FixedIdentity)` earns ***RepresentableFunctor***.

[FixedFunctor](fixed-functor.md) maps objects and morphisms, and
[FixedIdentity](fixed-identity.md) is the terminal identity on each fixed
object.  Their composition asserts that the functor’s action is determined by
its values on identities, matching representability.

title: Context Adjunction Witness
act: ContextAdjunctionWitness
slug: context-adjunction-witness
top: ContextFlow
bottom: ContextNucleus
summary: Witness the adjunction between the context flow and nucleus by letting the flow observe the nucleus.
tags:
- act
layer: act
status: plan
---
# Context Adjunction Witness

An adjunction between two functors is witnessed by a residuation isomorphism
between hom-sets.  `DynamicResiduation` expresses this relationship for
the context flow and nucleus, and we package it explicitly by composing the flow
with the nucleus:
`(ContextFlow ContextNucleus)` earns
***ContextAdjunctionWitness***.

The act states that maps out of a flowed context correspond to maps into a
closed context in the recognitional sense, exhibiting the adjunction
`ContextFlow ⊣ ContextNucleus`.

# Fixed Monad Unit

`FixedNucleateProfile` acts as a closure on fixed recognitions, and the monad
unit injects each recognition into its closure.  We witness this by letting the
identity observe the nucleus:
`(FixedIdentity FixedNucleateProfile)` earns
***FixedMonadUnit***.

[FixedIdentity](fixed-identity.md) gives the identity morphism on each fixed
object, and [FixedNucleateProfile](fixed-nucleate-profile.md) sends each
recognition to its fixed closure.  Their composition states that each object is
mapped into its closure via the identity, i.e. `(eta)_X : X → N(X)`.

tags:

---
# Dynamic Residuation

Dynamic residuation states that flowing a context and then testing implication
is equivalent to testing implication against a closed context.  We express this
by composing [FlowIndexImplication](flow-index-implication.md) with
[ContextGeometry](context-geometry.md):
`(FlowIndexImplication ContextGeometry)` earns
***DynamicResiduation***.

The act records that the law “`c ≤ a ⇒_F b` iff `F(c ∧ a) ≤ b`” continues to
hold when both sides are restricted to the context flow and nucleus.

# Fixed Flow Profile

`FlowProfile = (Flow ProfileRecognitions)` restricts the global flow to a given
profile.  To specialize this to the fixed-profile recognitions we let
[ShuffleFlow](shuffle-flow.md) witness
[FixedProfileRecognitions](fixed-profile-recognitions.md):
`(ShuffleFlow FixedProfileRecognitions)` earns
***FixedFlowProfile***.

`ShuffleFlow` evolves admissible trace-shuffle classes along evaluation
contexts, and `FixedProfileRecognitions` picks out recognitions stabilized by
the same dynamics and fixed shape.  The composition restricts the shuffle
flow to this profile, yielding a dynamics where every state evolves according to
that trace structure while preserving the fixed shape.

tags:

---
# Detailed Balance

To assert detailed balance, we require the flow–measure step
and its reverse to be observationally indistinguishable when weighted by the
stationary kernel.  We therefore let
[DetailedBalanceWitness](detailed-balance-witness.md) witness
[FlowMeasureStep](flow-measure-step.md):
`(DetailedBalanceWitness FlowMeasureStep)` earns
***DetailedBalance***.

`DetailedBalanceWitness` compares reverse transitions to forward ones
under observation, and `FlowMeasureStep` is the forward step.  Their composition
asserts that the two are equivalent after weighting by observations and
stabilization, which is exactly the detailed-balance condition internal to the
profile.

# Fixed Morphism

To treat the fixed profile as a category we need morphisms preserving the fixed
structure.  [Morph](morph.md) records structure-preserving maps between
recognitions, and [FixedProfileRecognitions](fixed-profile-recognitions.md)

`Morph` already preserves meets, joins, and implication, and restricting it via
the fixed recognitions ensures the resulting morphisms respect the same flow,
nucleus, and shape properties.

# Profile Kernel Step

A flow–measure kernel evolves fixed invariant states within a single profile.
To propagate these dynamics between profiles we use the profile tower
recognitions: [BuildProfileTower](build-profile-tower.md) maps physics,
semantics, and syntax upward through profiles.  Letting the kernel
witness this tower,
`(ObservationKernel BuildProfileTower)`, earns
***ProfileKernelStep***.

[ObservationKernel](observation-kernel.md) is the one-step operator on fixed
invariant states.  `BuildProfileTower` records how each layer of recognitions
reconstructs the next profile.  Their composition lifts an update from a profile
to its successor in the tower, giving the profile-level transition step.

# Reverse Flow–Measure Step

Detailed balance compares forward and reverse transitions.  The forward φ-step
is [FlowMeasureStep](flow-measure-step.md); the reverse uses the stationary
kernel applied backwards through the flow.  We therefore compose the stationary
kernel with the flow:
`(FixedKernel FixedFlowProfile)` earns
***ReverseFlowStep***.

[FixedKernel](fixed-kernel.md) is fixed under kernel updates, and
`FixedFlowProfile` is invertible up to nucleus and stabilization.  Their
composition yields the reverse step: the evolution that recovers the pre-image
up to stabilization.

# Witnessing ObservationEquivalence

## Interpretation

Contexts now witness stabilized equivalence acts, but we must cite them as observations.  *Recognize Observation* witnessing *Contextual Observation Equivalence* produces ***Witness Observation Equivalence*** ([WitnessObservationEquivalence](witness-observation-equivalence.md)).

The composition uses earned recognitions to cite the acts back into the observation layer, so *Witness Observation Equivalence* is valid.

  1. Profiling Shuffle-Stable Recognitions (ShuffleProfileRecognitions)
  • Path: docs/math/acts/shuffle-profile-recognitions.md
  • Status: plan
  • Top: FixFlowNucleus
  • Bottom: CollapseShuffle

Original

---
title: Profiling Shuffle-Stable Recognitions
act: ShuffleProfileRecognitions
slug: shuffle-profile-recognitions
top: FixFlowNucleus
bottom: CollapseShuffle
summary: Recognitions fixed by flow and nucleus and invariant under shuffle collapse witness the shuffle profile, so we let `FixFlowNucleus` observe `CollapseShuffle`.
tags:
- act
layer: act
status: plan
---
# Profiling Shuffle-Stable Recognitions

[FixFlowNucleus](fix-flow-nucleus.md) already records recognitions fixed by both
[Flow](flow.md) and [Nucleate](nucleate.md).  [CollapseShuffle](collapse-shuffle.md)
records which trace differences vanish under the nucleus: admissible shuffles.
To obtain the shuffle profile, we want recognitions that are simultaneously
flow–nucleus fixed and stable under identification of trace shuffles, so we let
`FixFlowNucleus` witness the shuffle collapse:
`(FixFlowNucleus CollapseShuffle)` earns
***ShuffleProfileRecognitions***.

Any recognition stabilized by flow and nucleus lies in `FixFlowNucleus`, and
`CollapseShuffle` identifies recognitions whose traces differ only by admissible
reordering.  The composition therefore picks out exactly those recognitions
whose stabilized form is invariant under (a) the global dynamics and closure,
and (b) the reordering of trace-progress steps.  These recognitions do not care
which admissible trace we used to reach them, so they define the shuffle
profile.

{{ act_nav(page.meta) }}
  1. Decomposing Trace (DecomposeTrace)
  • Path: docs/math/acts/decompose-trace.md
  • Status: plan
  • Top: HeadTrace
  • Bottom: TailTrace
  • Slug: decompose-trace

Original

---
title: Decomposing Trace
act: DecomposeTrace
slug: decompose-trace
top: HeadTrace
bottom: TailTrace
summary: Every completed trace splits uniquely into its leading head continuation and the remaining tail continuation, so we witness the recursive trace shape by composing the head and tail recognitions.
tags:
- act
layer: act
status: plan
---
# Decomposing Trace

`StartTrace`, `AdvanceTrace`, `ContinueTrace`, and `CompleteTrace` record how a
trace grows step by step, but nothing yet states the recursive *shape* of an
arbitrary completed trace.  The head–tail recognitions
([HeadTrace](head-trace.md), [TailTrace](tail-trace.md),
[TraceStep](trace-step.md), [ReheadTrace](rehead-trace.md),
[RetailTrace](retail-trace.md)) jointly witness the full record of
[CompleteTrace](complete-trace.md), so letting `HeadTrace` observe `TailTrace`
forces the decomposition of a trace into its left and right predecessors.

The composition `(HeadTrace TailTrace)` carries only previously earned data.
`HeadTrace` isolates the leading orientation of any completed trace while
`TailTrace` isolates the remainder, and the earlier recognitions ensure the tail
re-enters the trace (via `TraceStep`, `RenewTrace`, `ReheadTrace`,
`RetailTrace`) exactly as a shorter trace would.  Therefore
***DecomposeTrace*** witnesses the structural fact that every completed trace
splits into two smaller traces: the head’s continuation and the tail’s
continuation.


{{ act_info(page.meta) }}

# Retailing Trace

## Interpretation

After reheading, we let the act *Rehead Trace* witness the act *Tail Trace* to pin down the renewed tail.

The tree `(ReheadTrace TailTrace)` explicitly pairs *Rehead Trace* with *Tail Trace*, capturing the tail that accompanies the new head.  We call this act *Retail Trace*.

# Restepping Trace

## Interpretation

The renewed tail must rejoin the stepping process, so the act *Retail Trace* witnesses the act *Trace Step*.

In `(RetailTrace TraceStep)` the act *Retail Trace* observes *Trace Step*, recording the renewed tail re-entering the stepping act.  This is exactly what *Restep Trace* denotes.

# Shuffling Trace

Many trace acts commute: [ReheadTrace](rehead-trace.md) reorders against
[RetailTrace](retail-trace.md), [RestepTrace](restep-trace.md) reorders against
[TraceStep](trace-step.md), and each head/tail act commutes with the earlier
progressions exposed by [CompleteTrace](complete-trace.md).  No recognition yet
packages these commutations into a single principle, so we force the renewed
head to witness the stepping remainder: `(ReheadTrace RestepTrace)` earns
***ShuffleTrace***.

`ReheadTrace` and `RestepTrace` already demonstrate the two independent ways a
trace can progress: renewing the head or renewing the remainder.  Their
composition shows these progressions can be swapped without violating any
earned admissibility.  Thus `ShuffleTrace` records that the family of
trace-progressing acts forms a free shuffle algebra—any ordering built from
these steps is admissible, and admissibility is closed under permutation of
independent steps.
